func Covers(ownerRules, servantRules []rbacv1.PolicyRule) (bool, []rbacv1.PolicyRule) {\n28: \t// 1.  Break every servantRule into individual rule tuples: group, verb, resource, resourceName\n29: \t// 2.  Compare the mini-rules against each owner rule.  Because the breakdown is down to the most atomic level, we're guaranteed that each mini-servant rule will be either fully covered or not covered by a single owner rule\n30: \t// 3.  Any left over mini-rules means that we are not covered and we have a nice list of them.\n31: \t// TODO: it might be nice to collapse the list down into something more human readable\n32: \n33: \tsubrules := []rbacv1.PolicyRule{}\n34: \tfor _, servantRule := range servantRules {\n35: \t\tsubrules = append(subrules, BreakdownRule(servantRule)...)\n36: \t}\n37: \n38: \tuncoveredRules := \t\t\t\tcovered = true\n44: \t\t\t\tbreak\n45: \t\t\t}\n46: \t\t}\n47: \n48: \t\tif !covered {\n49: \t\t\tuncoveredRules = append(uncoveredRules, subrule)\n50: \t\t}\n51: \t}\n52: \n53: \treturn (len(uncoveredRules) == 0), uncoveredRules\n54: }\n55: \n56: // BreadownRule takes a rule and builds an equivalent list of rules that each have at most one verb, one\n57: // resource, and one resource name\n58: func BreakdownRule(rule rbacv1.PolicyRule) []rbacv1.PolicyRule {\n59: \tsubrules := []rbacv1.PolicyRule{}\n60: \tfor _, group := range rule.APIGroups {\n61: \t\tfor _, resource := range append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{APIGroups: []string{group}, Resources: []string{resource}, Verbs: []string{verb}, ResourceNames: []string{resourceName}})\n66: \t\t\t\t\t}\n67: \n68: \t\t\t\t} else {\n69: \t\t\t\t\tsubrules = append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{APIGroups: []string{group}, Resources: []string{resource}, Verbs: []string{verb}})\n70: \t\t\t\t}\n71: \n72: \t\t\t}\n73: \t\t}\n74: []string, ele string) bool {\n87: \tfor _, s := range set {\n88: \t\tif s == ele {\n89: \t\t\treturn true\n90: \t\t}\n91: \t}\n92: \treturn false\n93: }\n94: \n95: func hasAll(set, contains []string) bool {\n96: \towning := make(map[string]struct{}, len(set))\n97: \tfor _, ele := range set {\n98: \t\towning[ele] = struct{}{}\n99: \t}\n100: \tfor _, ele := range contains {\n101: \t\tif _, ok := owning[ele]; !ok {\n102: \t\t\treturn false\n103: \t\t}\n104: \t}\n105: \treturn true\n106: }\n107: \n108: func resourceCoversAll(setResources, coversResources []string) bool {\n109: \t// if we have a star or an exact match on all resources, then we match\n110: \tif has(setResources, rbacv1.ResourceAll) || hasAll(setResources, coversResources) {\n111: \t\treturn true\n112: \t}\n113: \n114: \tfor _, then we definitely don't match.  fail.\n120: \t\tif !strings.Contains(path, \"/\") {\n121: \t\t\treturn false\n122: \t\t}\n123: \t\ttokens := strings.SplitN(path, \"/\", 2)\n124: \t\tresourceToCheck := \"*/\" + tokens[1]\n125: \t\tif !has(setResources, resourceToCheck) {\n126: \t\t\treturn false\n127: \t\t}\n128: \t}\n129: \n130: \treturn true\n131: }\n132: \n133: func strings.HasPrefix(subPath, strings.TrimRight(ownerPath, \"*\"))\n154: }\n155: \n156: // ruleCovers determines whether the ownerRule (which may have multiple verbs, resources, and resourceNames) covers\n157: // the subrule (which may only contain at most one verb, resource, and resourceName)\n158: func ruleCovers(ownerRule, subRule rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n159: \tverbMatches := subRule.NonResourceURLs)\n163: \n164: \tresourceNameMatches := false\n165: \n166: \tif len(subRule.ResourceNames) == 0 {\n167: \t\tresourceNameMatches = (len(ownerRule.ResourceNames) == 0)\n168: \t} else {\n169: \t\tresourceNameMatches = (len(ownerRule.ResourceNames) == 0) || hasAll(ownerRule.ResourceNames, subRule.ResourceNames)\n170: \t}\n171: \n172: \treturn verbMatches && groupMatches && resourceMatches && resourceNameMatches && nonResourceURLMatches\n173: }\n174:
